# Task: Kubernetes APF QueueSet Deep-Dive

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce an algorithmic deep-dive on APF QueueSet behavior, dispatch flow, and fairness tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the APF QueueSet subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

## Summary of What's Included

The document provides:

1. **Subsystem Architecture** – Purpose, boundaries, and integration with APF Controller, APF Filter, metrics, and shuffle sharding.

2. **Core Components** (with code paths):
   - QueueSet interface and implementation
   - Queue and request structs
   - Two-phase construction pattern
   - Virtual time (R) progression mechanics

3. **End-to-End Request Flow**:
   - StartRequest() lifecycle with both bypass and queued paths
   - Virtual time synchronization formula and anti-overflow handling
   - Shuffle sharding queue assignment algorithm
   - Fair dispatch by virtual finish time
   - Request finish and seat release (including AdditionalLatency handling)

4. **Configuration & Reconfiguration** – Non-disruptive dynamic scaling of queues and concurrency limits

5. **Failure Modes & Design Tradeoffs**:
   - Rejection scenarios with metrics
   - Fairness guarantees (bounded divergence from ideal fair share)
   - Estimatedserviceduration heuristic and its implications
   - Edge cases (empty queues, SeatSeconds overflow, cancellation)

6. **Extension Points**:
   - Pluggable EventClock for virtual time customization
   - Promise factory for dispatch decisions
   - Metrics hooks and observability
   - Debug/Dump interface
   - Work estimator integration

7. **Operational Guidance**:
   - Key metrics for monitoring (rejections, dispatch rate, wait time, utilization, epoch advances)
   - Debugging scenarios with diagnosis steps
   - Capacity planning (queue count, depth, hand size)
   - Performance characteristics (lock contention, memory, virtual time

Creation, like\\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\\n33: \\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\\n34: \\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\\n35: \\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\\n36: \\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\\n37: \\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\\n38: \\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\\n39: \\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\\n40: \\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\\n41: \\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n42: }\\n43: \\n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\\n47: \\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\\n48: \\t// dispatching configuration.\\n49: \\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\\n54: // functionality described in the \\\"Assignment to a Queue\\\", \\\"Queuing\\\",\\n55: // and \\\"Dispatching\\\" sections of\\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\\n58: // today is not that day.\\n59: type QueueSet interface {\\n60: \\t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\\n61: \\t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\\n62: \\t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\\n63: \\t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\\n64: \\t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\\n65: \\t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\\n66: \\t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\\n67: \\t// and until it is undesired and empty.\\n68: \\tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n69: \\n70: \\t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\\n71: \\t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\\n72: \\t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\\n73: \\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\\n74: \\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\\n75: \\t// from false to true.\\n76: \\tIsIdle() bool\\n77: \\n78: \\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\\n79: \\t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\\n80: \\t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\\n81: \\t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\\n82: \\t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\\n83: \\t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\\n84: \\t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\\n85: \\t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\\n86: \\t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\\n87: \\t// was idle at the moment of the return.     "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package fairqueuing\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"context\"\n21: \n22: \t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/debug\"\n23: \t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics\"\n24: \t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request\"\n25: )\n26: \n27: // QueueSetFactory is used to create QueueSet objects.  Creation, like\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\n33: \t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\n34: \t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\n35: \t// execution covering just the regular phase.\n36: \t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\n37: \t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\n38: \t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\n39: \t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\n40: \t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\n41: \tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n42: }\n43: \n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\n47: \t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\n48: \t// dispatching configuration.\n49: \tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n50: }\n51: \n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\n54: // functionality described in the \"Assignment to a Queue\", \"Queuing\",\n55: // and \"Dispatching\" sections of\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\n58: // today is not that day.\n59: type QueueSet interface {\n60: \t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\n61: \t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\n62: \t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\n63: \t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\n64: \t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\n65: \t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\n66: \t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\n67: \t// and until it is undesired and empty.\n68: \tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n69: \n70: \t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\n71: \t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\n72: \t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\n73: \t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\n74: \t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\n75: \t// from false to true.\n76: \tIsIdle() bool\n77: \n78: \t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\n79: \t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\n80: \t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\n81: \t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\n82: \t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\n83: \t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\n84: \t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\n85: \t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\n86: \t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\n87: \t// was idle at the moment of the return. You can find a good paper\\n23: // on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\\n24: // http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\\n25: // and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\\n26: // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\\n27: //\\n28: // Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\\n29: // queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\\n30: // requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\\n31: // link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\\n32: // service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\\n33: // completes.\\n34: //\\n35: // The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\\n36: // adaptation of the concept called \\\"R(t)\\\" in the original paper and\\n37: // \\\"virtual time\\\" in the implementation outline. In that\\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper\u2019s terms, \\\"R(t)\\\" is the\\n40: // number of \\\"rounds\\\" that have been completed at real time t ---\\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \\\"in\\\" its queue until the\\n45: // packet\u2019s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\\n53: // respect to t is\\n54: //\\n55: //\\t1 / NEQ(t) .\\n56: //\\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\\n59: //\\n60: //\\tC / NEQ(t) .\\n61: //\\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\\n63: // execute. The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\\n72: //\\n73: //\\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\\n74: //\\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\\n77: // real nanosecond). The fields listed before the lock\n71: // should not be changed; the fields listed after the\n72: // lock must be accessed only while holding the lock.\n73: //\n74: // The methods of this type follow the naming convention that the\n75: // suffix \"Locked\" means the caller must hold the lock; for a method\n76: // whose name does not end in \"Locked\" either acquires the lock or\n77: // does not care about locking.\n78: //\n79: // The methods of this type also follow the convention that the suffix\n80: // \"ToBoundLocked\" means that the caller may have to follow up with a\n81: // call to `boundNextDispatchLocked`. \t\t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n321: \t\t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"concurrency-limit\")\n322: \t\t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n323: \t\t}\n324: \t\treq = qs.dispatchSansQueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n325: \t\treturn req, false\n326: \t}\n327: \n328: \t// ========================================================================\n329: \t// Step 1:\n330: \t// 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n331: \t// 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n332: \t// we are at max queue length\n333: \t// 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n334: \treq = qs.shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2, queueNoteFn)\n335: \t// req == nil means that the request was rejected - no remaining\n336: \t// concurrency shares and at max queue length already\n337: \tif req == nil {\n338: \t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): rejecting request %q %#+v %#+v due to queue full\", qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n339: \t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n340: \t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"queue-full\")\n341: \t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n342: \t}\n343: \n344: \t// ========================================================================\n345: \t// Step 2:\n346: \t// The next step is to invoke the method that dequeues as much\n347: \t// as possible.\n348: \t// This method runs a loop, as long as there are non-empty\n349: \t// queues and the number currently executing is less than the\n350: \t// assured concurrency value.  The body of the loop uses the\n351: \t// fair queuing technique to pick a queue and dispatch a\n352: \t// request from that queue.\n353: \tqs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n354: \n355: \treturn req, false\n356: }\n357: \n358: // ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory is the promiseFactoryFactory that\n359: // a queueSetFactory would ordinarily use.\n360: // Test code might use something different.\n361: func ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory(qs *queueSet) promiseFactory {\n362: \treturn promise.NewWriteOnce\n363: }\n364: \n365: // MaxSeats returns the maximum number of seats this request requires, it is\n366: // the maxumum of the two - WorkEstimate.InitialSeats, WorkEstimate.FinalSeats.\n367: func (req *request) MaxSeats() int {\n368: \treturn req.workEstimate.MaxSeats()\n369: }\n370: \n371: func (req *request) InitialSeats() int {\n372: \treturn int(req.workEstimate.InitialSeats)\n373: }\n374: \n375: func (req *request) NoteQueued(inQueue bool) {\n376: \tif req.queueNoteFn != nil {\n377: \t\treq.queueNoteFn(inQueue)\n378: \t}\n379: }\n380: \n381: func (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n382: \texec, idle := req.wait()\n383: \tif !exec {\n384: \t\treturn idle\n385: \t}\n386: \tfunc() {\n387: \t\tdefer func() {\n388: \t\t\tidle = req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n389: \t\t}()\n390: \n391: \t\texecFn()\n392: \t}()\n393: \n394: \treturn idle\n395: }\n396: \n397: func (req *request) wait() (bool, bool) {\n398: \tqs := req.qs\n399: \n400: \t// ========================================================================\n401: \t// Step 3:\n402: \t// The final step is to wait on a decision from\n403: \t// somewhere and then act on it.\n404: \tdecisionAny := req.decision.Get()\n405: \tqs.lockAndSyncTime(req.ctx)\n406: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n407: \tif req.waitStarted {\n408: \t\t// This can not happen, because the client is forbidden to\n409: \t\t// call Wait twice on the same request\n410: \t\tklog.Errorf(\"Duplicate call to the Wait method!  Immediately returning execute=false.  QueueSet=%s, startTime=%s, descr1=%#+v, descr2=%#+v\", req.qs.qCfg.Name, req.startTime, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n411: \t\treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n412: \t}\n413: \treq.waitStarted = true\n414: \tswitch decisionAny {\n415: \tcase decisionCancel: // handle in code following this switch\n416: \tcase decisionExecute:\n417: \t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Dispatching request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n418: \t\treturn true, false\n419: \tdefault:\n420: \t\t// This can not happen, all possible values are handled above\n421: \t\tklog.Errorf(\"QS(%s): Impossible decision (type %T, value %#+v) for request %#+v %#+v!  Treating as cancel\", qs.qCfg.Name, decisionAny, decisionAny, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n422: \t}\n423: \t// TODO(aaron-prindle) add metrics for this case\n424: \tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Ejecting request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n425: \t// remove the request from the queue as its queue wait time has exceeded\n426: \tqueue := req.queue\n427: \tif req.removeFromQueueLocked() != nil {\n428: \t\tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n429: \t\tqs.totRequestsWaiting--\n430: \t\tqs.totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n431: \t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n432: \t\tqs.totRequestsCancelled++\n433: \t\tmetrics.AddReject(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, \"time-out\")\n434: \t\tmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -1)\n435: \t\tmetrics.AddSeatsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -req.MaxSeats())\n436: \t\treq.NoteQueued(false)\n437: \t\tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.Add(-1)\n438: \t\tqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n439: \t}\n440: \treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n441: }\n442: \n443: func (qs *queueSet) IsIdle() bool {\n444: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n445: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n446: \treturn qs.isIdleLocked()\n447: }\n448: \n449: func (qs *queueSet) isIdleLocked() bool {\n450: \treturn qs.totRequestsWaiting == 0 && qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0\n451: }\n452: \n453: // lockAndSyncTime acquires the lock and updates the virtual time.\n454: // Doing them together avoids the mistake of modifying some queue state\n455: // before calling syncTimeLocked.\n456: func (qs *queueSet) lockAndSyncTime(ctx context.Context) {\n457: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n458: \tqs.syncTimeLocked(ctx)\n459: }\n460: \n461: // syncTimeLocked updates the virtual time based on the assumption\n462: // that the current state of the queues has been in effect since\n463: // `qs.lastRealTime`.  Thus, it should be invoked after acquiring the\n464: // lock and before modifying the state of any queue.\n465: func (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n466: \trealNow := qs.clock.Now()\n467: \ttimeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n468: \tqs.lastRealTime = realNow\n469: \tprevR := qs.currentR\n470: \tincrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n471: \tqs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n472: \tswitch {\n473: \tcase prevR > qs.currentR:\n474: \t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queueset::currentR overflow\"), \"Overflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", realNow.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"prevR\", prevR, \"incrR\", incrR, \"currentR\", qs.currentR)\n475: \tcase qs.currentR >= highR:\n476: \t\tqs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n477: \t}\n478: \tmetrics.SetCurrentR(qs.qCfg.Name, qs.currentR.ToFloat())\n479: }\n480: \n481: // rDecrement is the amount by which the progress meter R is wound backwards\n482: // when needed to avoid overflow.\n483: const rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\n484: \n485: // highR is the threshold that triggers advance of the epoch.\n486: // That is, decrementing the global progress meter R by rDecrement.\n487: const highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n488: \n489: // advanceEpoch subtracts rDecrement from the global progress meter R\n490: // and all the readings that have been taked from that meter.\n491: // The now and incrR parameters are only used to add info to the log messages.\n492: func (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n493: \toldR := qs.currentR\n494: \tqs.currentR -= rDecrement\n495: \tklog.InfoS(\"Advancing epoch\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", now.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"oldR\", oldR, \"newR\", qs.currentR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n496: \tsuccess := true\n497: \tfor qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n498: \t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n499: \t\t\t// Do not just decrement, the value could be quite outdated.\n500: \t\t\t// It is safe to reset to zero in this case, because the next request\n501: \t\t\t// will overwrite the zero with `qs.currentR`.\n502: \t\t\tqueue.nextDispatchR = 0\n503: \t\t\tcontinue\n504: \t\t}\n505: \t\toldNextDispatchR := queue.nextDispatchR\n506: \t\tqueue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n507: \t\tif queue.nextDispatchR > oldNextDispatchR {\n508: \t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queue::nextDispatchR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"oldNextDispatchR\", oldNextDispatchR, \"newNextDispatchR\", queue.nextDispatchR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n509: \t\t\tsuccess = false\n510: \t\t}\n511: \t\tqueue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n512: \t\t\toldArrivalR := req.arrivalR\n513: \t\t\treq.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n514: \t\t\tif req.arrivalR > oldArrivalR {\n515: \t\t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"request::arrivalR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"request\", *req, \"oldArrivalR\", oldArrivalR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n516: \t\t\t\tsuccess = false\n517: \t\t\t}\n518: \t\t\treturn true\n519: \t\t})\n520: \t}\n521: \tmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)\n522: }\n523: \n524: // getVirtualTimeRatio calculates the rate at which virtual time has\n525: // been advancing, according to the logic in `doc.go`.\n526: func (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n527: \tactiveQueues := 0\n528: \tseatsRequested := 0\n529: \tfor _, queue := range qs.queues {\n530: \t\t// here we want the sum of the maximum width of the requests in this queue since our\n531: \t\t// goal is to find the maximum rate at which the queue could work.\n532: \t\tseatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n533: \t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n534: \t\t\tactiveQueues++\n535: \t\t}\n536: \t}\n537: \tif activeQueues == 0 {\n538: \t\treturn 0\n539: \t}\n540: \treturn math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n541: }\n542: \n543: // shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked encapsulates the logic required\n544: // to validate and enqueue a request for the queueSet/QueueSet:\n545: // 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n546: // 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n547: // we are at max queue length\n548: // 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n549: // returns the enqueud request on a successful enqueue\n550: // returns nil in the case that there is no available concurrency or\n551: // the queuelengthlimit has been reached\n552: func (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) *request {\n553: \t// Start with the shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n554: \tqueueIdx := qs.shuffleShardLocked(hashValue, descr1, descr2)\n555: \tqueue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n556: \n557: \tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n558: \n559: \t// Create a request and enqueue\n560: \treq := &request{\n561: \t\tqs:                qs,\n562: \t\tfsName:            fsName,\n563: \t\tflowDistinguisher: flowDistinguisher,\n564: \t\tctx:               ctx,\n565: \t\tdecision:          qs.promiseFactory(nil, ctx, decisionCancel),\n566: \t\tarrivalTime:       qs.clock.Now(),\n567: \t\tarrivalR:          qs.currentR,\n568: \t\tqueue: \t}\n574: \tif ok := qs.rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(req); !ok {\n575: \t\treturn nil\n576: \t}\n577: \tmetrics.ObserveQueueLength(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, queue.requestsWaiting.Length())\n578: \treturn req\n579: }\n580: \n581: // shuffleShardLocked uses shuffle sharding to select a queue index\n582: // using the given hashValue and the shuffle sharding parameters of the queueSet.\n583: func (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardLocked(hashValue uint64, descr1, descr2 interface{}) int {\n584: \tvar backHand [8]int\n585: \t// Deal into a data structure, so that the order of visit below is not necessarily the order of the deal.\n586: \t// This removes bias in the case of flows with overlapping hands.\n587: \thand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\n588: \thandSize := len(hand)\n589: \toffset := qs.enqueues % handSize\n590: \tqs.enqueues++\n591: \tbestQueueIdx := -1\n592: \tminQueueSeatSeconds := fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds\n593: \tfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n594: \t\tqueueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n595: \t\tqueue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n596: \t\tqueueSum := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum()\n597: \n598: \t\t// this is the total amount of work in seat-seconds for requests\n599: \t\t// waiting in this queue, we will select the queue with the minimum.\n600: \t\tthisQueueSeatSeconds := queueSum.TotalWorkSum\n601: \t\tklog.V(7).Infof(\"QS(%s): For request %#+v %#+v considering queue %d with sum: %#v and %d seats in use, nextDispatchR=%v\", qs.qCfg.Name, descr1, descr2, queueIdx, queueSum, queue.seatsInUse, queue.nextDispatchR)\n602: \t\tif thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n603: \t\t\tminQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n604: \t\t\tbestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n605: \t\t}\n606: \t}\n607: \tif klogV := klog.V(6); klogV.Enabled() {\n608: \t\tchosenQueue := qs.queues[bestQueueIdx]\n609: \t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: For request %#+v %#+v chose queue %d, with sum: %#v & %d seats in use & nextDispatchR=%v\", qs.qCfg.Name, qs.clock.Now().Format(nsTimeFmt), qs.currentR, descr1, descr2, bestQueueIdx, chosenQueue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum(), chosenQueue.seatsInUse, chosenQueue.nextDispatchR)\n610: \t}\n611: \treturn bestQueueIdx\n612: }\n613: \n614: // rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked rejects or enqueues the newly arrived\n615: // request, which has been assigned to a queue.  If up against the\n616: // queue length limit and the concurrency limit then returns false.\n617: // Otherwise enqueues and returns true.\n618: func (qs *queueSet) rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(request *request) bool {\n619: \tqueue := request.queue\n620: \tcurQueueLength := queue.requestsWaiting.Length()\n621: \t// rejects the newly arrived request if resource criteria not met\n622: \tif qs.totSeatsInUse >= qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n623: \t\tcurQueueLength >= qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit {\n624: \t\treturn false\n625: \t}\n626: \n627: \tqs.enqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n628: \treturn \t\tklogV := klog.V(6)\n639: \t\tif klogV.Enabled() {\n640: \t\t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: initialized queue %d start R due to request %#+v %#+v\", qs.qCfg.Name, now.Format(nsTimeFmt), dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() {\n655: \tfor qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 && qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit && qs.dispatchLocked() {\n656: \t}\n657: }\n658: \n659: func (qs *queueSet) metrics.SetDispatchMetrics because there is no queuing and thus no interesting virtual world\n661: \tnow := qs.clock.Now()\n662: \treq := &request{\n663: \t\tqs:                qs,\n664: \t\tfsName:            fsName,\n665: \t\tflowDistinguisher: flowDistinguisher,\n666: \t\tctx:               ctx,\n667: \t\tstartTime:         now,\n668: \t\tdecision:          qs.promiseFactory(decisionExecute, The\n692: // return value indicates whether a request was dequeued; this will\n693: // be false when either all queues are empty or the request at the head\n694: // of the next queue cannot be dispatched.\n695: func (qs *queueSet) dispatchLocked() bool {\n696: \tqueue, request := qs.findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n697: \tif queue == nil {\n698: \t\treturn false\n699: \t}\n700: \tif request == nil { // This should never happen. \tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsExecuting.Add(1)\n727: \tqs.execSeatsGauge.Add(float64(request.MaxSeats()))\n728: \tqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n729: \tklogV := klog.V(6)\n730: \tif klogV.Enabled() {\n731: \t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: dispatching request %#+v %#+v work %v from queue %d with start R %v, queue will have %d waiting & %d requests \t\t\trequest.workEstimate, queue.index, queue.nextDispatchR)\n740: \t}\n741: \tqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n742: \treturn true\n743: }\n744: \n745: // canAccommodateSeatsLocked returns qs.qCfg.Name)\n809: \t\treturn nil, nil\n810: \t}\n811: \tif !qs.canAccommodateSeatsLocked(oldestReqFromMinQueue.MaxSeats()) {\n812: \t\t// since we have not picked the queue with the minimum virtual with %#v waiting & %d requests occupying %d seats\",\n923: \t\t\t\t\tqs.qCfg.Name, now.Format(nsTimeFmt), qs.currentR, r.descr1, r.descr2, r.workEstimate.FinalSeats, r.queue.index,\n924:   "content": "# API Priority and Fairness QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet is a sophisticated fair queuing subsystem that implements **fair queuing for server requests**, adapting networking fair queuing algorithms to API server concurrency management. It enforces per-priority-level concurrency limits while ensuring that no flow of requests can starve others, even under load. The system uses virtual time tracking, shuffle sharding for queue assignment, and seat-based resource accounting to provide both isolation and fairness.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\nThe QueueSet subsystem serves one core responsibility: **manage queuing and dispatch of requests for a single Priority Level Configuration** in the APF system. Given a concurrency limit (seat count) and a desired number of queues, QueueSet decides:\n- Which requests get seats to execute immediately\n- Which requests enter a queue to wait\n- Which requests are rejected (queue full, no available seats)\n- When queued requests are dispatched in what order (fair order based on virtual finish time)\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies** (what feeds into QueueSet):\n- **APF Controller** (`apf_controller.go`): Manages FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects; creates and reconfigures QueueSets based on config changes.\n- **APF Filter** (`apf_filter.go`): Receives HTTP requests, classifies them via FlowSchemas, then calls QueueSet.StartRequest() to begin queuing/dispatch process.\n- **Request Work Estimator** (`request/width.go`): Computes WorkEstimate (InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency) for each request, describing its resource footprint.\n\n**Downstream Dependencies** (what QueueSet coordinates with):\n- **Metrics** (`metrics/`): Observes queuing depth, execution counts, seat utilization, dispatch virtual times.\n- **Shuffle Sharding** (`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding`): Distributes hash of request flow identifier across queues to prevent head-of-line blocking.\n- **Promise/WriteOnce** (`fairqueuing/promise/`): Asynchronous dispatch decision mechanism\u2014decision is set once a request is dequeued, multiple goroutines can await it.\n- **Event Clock** (`fairqueuing/eventclock/`): Provides virtual time progression and EventAfterDuration callbacks for seat release scheduling.\n\n**Not Included** (outside this subsystem):\n- Priority level allocation, borrowing, or rebalancing across priority levels (handled by `apf_controller.go`).\n- FlowSchema-to-PriorityLevel matching (handled by `apf_filter.go`).\n- Enforcement at transport/network layer.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 QueueSet Interface\n\n**Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go:59\u2013110`\n\nThe public contract exposed by one QueueSet instance:\n- **`StartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, ...)`** \u2192 `(Request, idle bool)`: Begin request handling. Returns either:\n  - Non-nil `Request` object to be finished later, or\n  - `nil` if immediately rejected (queue full OR no concurrency available).\n- **`BeginConfigChange(queuingConfig)`** \u2192 `QueueSetCompleter`: Start two-phase reconfiguration (separate queuing validation from dispatching commitment).\n- **`IsIdle()`** \u2192 `bool`: Check if QueueSet has zero queued and zero executing requests.\n- **`Dump(includeRequestDetails)`** \u2192 `debug.QueueSetDump`: Snapshot internal state for debugging.\n\n### 2.2 QueueSet Implementation Structure\n\n**Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\n#### 2.2.1 queueSet struct (lines 85\u2013167)\n\nCore state machine for one priority level:\n\n**Immutable Fields (initialized once):**\n- `clock`: EventClock for virtual time progression and callbacks.\n- `estimatedServiceDuration`: Default guess (3ms) for request service time; used to compute initial virtual finish times.\n- `promiseFactory`: Creates WriteOnce promises for dispatch decisions.\n- Gauge/metrics observers for tracking requests and seats.\n\n**Mutable Fields (protected by lock):**\n- `qCfg`: Current QueuingConfig (DesiredNumQueues, QueueLengthLimit, HandSize).\n- `dCfg`: Current DispatchingConfig (ConcurrencyLimit, denominator for metrics).\n- `queues`: Slice of `*queue` objects; length may exceed desired during drain.\n- `currentR`: **Virtual time (seat-seconds)** tracking progress through the system; increments based on concurrency and active queues.\n- `lastRealTime`: Real wall-clock time of last virtual time sync.\n- `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`, `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`: Aggregate counts.\n- `robinIndex`: Round-robin position for dispatch queue selection.\n- Counters: `enqueues`, `totRequestsDispatched`, `totRequestsRejected`, `totRequestsTimedout`, `totRequestsCancelled`.\n\n#### 2.2.2 queue struct (lines 93\u2013110)\n\nOne FIFO queue within a QueueSet:\n\n- `requestsWaiting`: FIFO list of waiting requests.\n- `requestsExecuting`: Set of currently executing requests from this queue.\n- `nextDispatchR`: Virtual start time for the **next** request to be dispatched from this queue. Updated as requests are dispatched or finish.\n- `seatsInUse`: Count of seats occupied by executing requests in this queue.\n- `index`: Position in parent QueueSet's queue array.\n\n#### 2.2.3 request struct (lines 33\u201383 in types.go)\n\nTransient wrapper for request-specific data:\n\n- `ctx`: Request context (carries cancellation, deadlines, user info).\n- `queue`: Pointer to its assigned queue (nil if bypass-queued).\n- `decision`: WriteOnce promise; initially set to decisionCancel, replaced with decisionExecute when dequeued.\n- `arrivalTime`, `arrivalR`: Real and virtual time of arrival.\n- `startTime`: Real time when request began executing.\n- `workEstimate`: WorkEstimate object (InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency, pre-computed total/final work in seat-seconds).\n- `removeFromQueueLocked`: Closure to remove this request from its FIFO.\n- Flow metadata: `flowDistinguisher`, `fsName` (for metrics/logging).\n\n#### 2.2.4 QueueSetFactory and two-phase construction\n\n**Location:** lines 40\u2013227 in queueset.go\n\nTwo-phase creation separates **queuing validation** (resource-light) from **dispatching commitment** (reserves concurrency):\n\n1. **`BeginConstruction(queuingConfig, metrics...)`**: Validates QueuingConfig, creates a shufflesharding.Dealer.\n   - Returns `QueueSetCompleter` if valid, error if QueuingConfig (DesiredNumQueues, HandSize) is invalid.\n2. **`Complete(dispatchingConfig)`**: Finalizes with concurrency limit. If this is the first completion, creates the QueueSet struct; otherwise reconfigures existing one.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow and Virtual Time Mechanics\n\n### 3.1 Request Arrival: StartRequest() Flow\n\n**Entry Point:** `queueSet.StartRequest()` (lines 308\u2013356)\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 StartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, flowDistinguisher, fsName, ...)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Lock + syncTime (update currentR based on elapsed time and active queues)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 [BYPASS PATH] If DesiredNumQueues < 1 (no queuing mode):\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If !canAccommodateSeats, reject immediately.\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 Otherwise, dispatchSansQueueLocked(): create request, mark executing, return it.\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 [QUEUED PATH] If DesiredNumQueues \u2265 1:\n   \u251c\u2500 shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(workEstimate, hashValue, ...):\n   \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Use hashValue to shuffle-shard into a queue (min-load queue from hand size).\n   \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Check if queue length + concurrency limits allow enqueue.\n   \u2502  \u2514\u2500 If yes: enqueue request, set decision promise to initial state (decisionCancel).\n   \u2502     If no: return nil (reject).\n   \u2502\n   \u2514\u2500 dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked():\n      \u2514\u2500 Loop: while requests waiting and seats < concurrency limit:\n         \u2514\u2500 findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked():\n            \u251c\u2500 Round-robin over queues, find one with oldest waiting request.\n            \u251c\u2500 Select queue with minimum virtual finish time (nextDispatchR + oldest.totalWork()).\n            \u2514\u2500 Return selected queue and request.\n         \u2514\u2500 Dequeue that request, set decision.Set(decisionExecute), move to executing.\n```\n\n### 3.2 Virtual Time (R) Progression\n\n**Key Insight:** Virtual time advances as a function of **concurrency and active queue count**, not real time.\n\n**Sync Logic** (`syncTimeLocked()` lines 465\u2013479):\n\nAt each lock acquisition:\n```\ntimeSinceLast = clock.Now() - lastRealTime\nincrR = SeatsTimesDuration(\n    getVirtualTimeRatio(),  // C / NEQ(t)\n    timeSinceLast\n)\ncurrentR += incrR\n```\n\n**Virtual Time Ratio** (`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()` lines 526\u2013541):\n\n```\nactiveQueues = count(queues with waiting or executing requests)\nseatsRequested = sum(seats in use + max seats of waiting requests in each queue)\nratio = min(seatsRequested, concurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\n**Intuition:**\n- If all C seats are occupied and NEQ queues are active, virtual time advances at rate C/NEQ per real nanosecond, so each queue \"gets\" 1/NEQ of seat-time per real time unit.\n- If only 3 queues are active with 2 seats requested each, virtual time advances at 6/3 = 2 per real ns.\n- When idle (activeQueues=0), ratio is 0; virtual time does not advance.\n\n**Epoch Management** (lines 481\u2013522):\n\nTo prevent SeatSeconds overflow (uint64), when currentR approaches `highR \u2248 MaxSeatSeconds/2 + MaxSeatSeconds/4`, `advanceEpoch()` subtracts a constant `rDecrement` from:\n- currentR\n- All queue.nextDispatchR\n- All request.arrivalR\n\nThis is an **anti-overflow mechanism**; virtual time is relative and shifting it uniformly preserves fairness.\n\n### 3.3 Queue Assignment: Shuffle Sharding\n\n**Location:** `shuffleShardLocked()` (lines 583\u2013612)\n\nShuffle sharding distributes flows across queues to prevent head-of-line blocking:\n\n```\nhand = dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\n// hand is a small subset (HandSize) of queues, randomized based on hash.\n\n// Among the hand, select the queue with minimum total work waiting.\noffset = enqueues % len(hand)\nbestQueue = hand with min(TotalWorkSum)\n```\n\n**Why this matters:**\n- If many flows hash to the same queue, they don't all block each other.\n- With HandSize \u2248 sqrt(DesiredNumQueues), even with worst-case hash collisions, impact is limited.\n- Tested extensively (queueset_test.go) to ensure fairness across scenarios.\n\n### 3.4 Dispatch and Fair Ordering\n\n**Dispatch Selection** (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` lines 776\u2013844):\n\nQueues are examined in round-robin order. The first queue with a waiting request has that request's virtual finish time computed:\n\n```\nvirtualFinishTime = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n```\n\n**The queue with the minimum virtualFinishTime is selected.** This implements **weighted fair queuing**: requests from queues with earlier virtual finish times are prioritized.\n\n**Anti-Windup Hack** (`boundNextDispatchLocked()` lines 952\u2013964):\n\nAfter dequeuing or when a queue's state changes, ensure:\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR >= min(arrivals in queue)\n```\n\nThis prevents a queue from getting a \"head start\" if it can't use all allocated seats, which would unfairly advance it in virtual time.\n\n### 3.5 Request Execution and Finish\n\n**Finish Phase** (`request.Finish(execFn)` lines 381\u2013395, `wait()` lines 397\u2013441):\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 Finish(execFn):\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 wait(): block on decision promise until dequeued or context deadline.\n\u2502  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 If decisionExecute: record startTime, return (execute=true, idle=false).\n\u2502  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 If decisionCancel: remove from queue, return (execute=false, idle=?).\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 If execute=true: call execFn() in a deferred cleanup context.\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req):\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 finishRequestLocked(req):\n\u2502     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Decrement totRequestsExecuting, totSeatsInUse.\n\u2502     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Adjust queue.nextDispatchR backward if actual service time < estimated:\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502   nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedDuration - actualDuration)\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502   (This credits the queue for \"unused\" virtual time.)\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2514\u2500 If AdditionalLatency > 0:\n\u2502     \u2502     \u251c\u2500 Schedule EventAfterDuration callback to release final seats.\n\u2502     \u2502     \u2502   (Final seats are held for AdditionalLatency after request finishes.)\n\u2502     \u2502     \u2514\u2500 This hides the extra latency from the user.\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked(): try to dispatch more queued requests.\n```\n\n**Work Estimation** (`types.go` lines 131\u2013146):\n\nTotal work is split into initial and final phases:\n```\ninitialWork = SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedServiceDuration)\nfinalWork   = SeatsTimesDuration(FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency)\ntotalWork   = initialWork + finalWork\n```\n\nThis allows pipelining: while one request is in its final phase (e.g., flushing response), another can begin initial phase.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Configuration and Reconfiguration\n\n### 4.1 Two-Phase Reconfiguration\n\n**Location:** `setConfiguration()` (lines 254\u2013287)\n\nWhen APF config changes:\n```\nBeginConfigChange(qCfg) \u2192 QueueSetCompleter\n  \u2514\u2500 checkConfig(qCfg): validate DesiredNumQueues, HandSize \u2192 error or Dealer\nComplete(dCfg) \u2192 reconfigured QueueSet\n  \u2514\u2500 setConfiguration():\n     \u251c\u2500 If DesiredNumQueues increases: create new queues, append to queues slice.\n     \u2502   (Request shard-sharding will assign to new queues on next request.)\n     \u251c\u2500 If DesiredNumQueues decreases: leave existing queues; they drain by attrition.\n     \u2502   (When queue becomes empty and count > desired, remove it.)\n     \u251c\u2500 Update qCfg, dCfg, dealer.\n     \u251c\u2500 Recalibrate metrics denominators (RequestsWaiting / (QLL * DesiredNumQueues)).\n     \u2514\u2500 dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked(): trigger pending dispatch.\n```\n\n**Key Property:** Configuration changes are **non-disruptive**. Existing queued/executing requests are unaffected.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Rejection Scenarios\n\nA request is rejected if:\n\n1. **Concurrency Limit Hit + Queue Full**\n   `qs.totSeatsInUse >= dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit && curQueueLength >= qCfg.QueueLengthLimit`\n   - Metrics: `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total{reason=\"queue-full\"}`\n\n2. **No-Queueing Mode, No Concurrency**\n   `DesiredNumQueues < 1 && !canAccommodateSeats(workEstimate.MaxSeats())`\n   - Metrics: `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total{reason=\"concurrency-limit\"}`\n\n3. **Context Deadline Exceeded While Queued**\n   Request waiting in queue; `decision.Get()` returns `decisionCancel` because context expires.\n   - Metrics: `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total{reason=\"time-out\"}`\n\n### 5.2 Fairness Guarantees and Tradeoffs\n\n#### Guarantee: Bounded Divergence from Ideal Fair Share\n\nIn traditional fair queuing, the bound is **one packet per flow**. In APF QueueSet:\n- Bound is **C requests** (concurrency limit) per queue.\n- A single queue can execute up to C requests concurrently.\n- With multiple queues and round-robin dispatch selection, fairness across queues is enforced by virtual finish time.\n\n**Tradeoff:** Shuffle sharding with HandSize < DesiredNumQueues trades perfect isolation for simplicity. With K queues and hand size H, a single flow contends with at most H-1 other flows in its subset. This is a probabilistic guarantee tuned by configuration.\n\n#### Estimated Service Duration: A Hardcoded Assumption\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration = 3 * time.Millisecond` (line 215)\n\n- Used to compute initial virtual work of a request before actual service time is known.\n- Once actual service time S is observed, virtual time is retroactively adjusted by (G - S).\n- **Tradeoff:** If G is too high, queues get under-credited initially and must wait; if too low, they get over-credited and monopolize virtual time early on. The 3ms default is a heuristic for read-only requests; write estimators use different logic.\n\n#### Queue Depth Limit and Rejection Logic\n\n`QueueLengthLimit` is **per-queue**, not global.\n- With Q queues, max waiting = Q * QueueLengthLimit.\n- **Tradeoff:** Allows tuning of acceptable queue depth without global synchronization, but doesn't directly cap total resource consumption (memory for request objects).\n\n### 5.3 Edge Cases and Anti-Patterns\n\n1. **Empty Queues and Virtual Time Stall**\n   If all queues are empty, `getVirtualTimeRatio()` returns 0, so virtual time does not advance.\n   - Consequence: when the first request arrives, it gets `arrivalR = currentR`, and if the queue was idle, `nextDispatchR` is reset to `currentR`, so the request is dispatched immediately.\n   - **Not a problem:** the algorithm is designed to handle this.\n\n2. **SeatSeconds Overflow**\n   Despite uint64 being huge (~585 years at 1 ns/tick), `advanceEpoch()` is called whenever `currentR >= highR` to prevent overflow.\n   - Metric: `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` tracks how many times this happens.\n   - **Operational concern:** A very long-lived apiserver with high concurrency could theoretically advance epochs frequently, but this is expected and non-disruptive.\n\n3. **Request Cancellation vs. Timeout**\n   Both map to `decisionCancel`. If a request's context is cancelled by the client or deadline is reached, `decision.Get()` returns the doneVal (decisionCancel).\n   - Unlike timeouts (which are dequeued when the request times out), context cancellation could occur while the request is executing.\n   - **Not a problem:** The promise is set only once; if `Finish()` is called after cancellation, it reads the already-set decision.\n\n4. **Adapting FinalSeats if They Exceed Limit**\n   In `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` (lines 827\u2013832), if FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit, they are clamped and AdditionalLatency is extended to preserve total work.\n   - **Rationale:** Ensures no request requires more seats than the total limit.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 EventClock and Virtual Time Customization\n\n**Location:** `fairqueuing/eventclock/`\n\nThe `eventclock.Interface` allows plugging in custom clocks:\n- `Real{}`: Uses system clock (production).\n- Test clocks: Can freeze time, advance manually, track callback scheduling.\n\n**Extension Use:** Tests can validate virtual time progression and epoch advancement without real delays.\n\n### 6.2 Promise Factory\n\n**Location:** lines 47\u201354 in queueset.go\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(...) promise.WriteOnce\ntype promiseFactoryFactory func(*queueSet) promiseFactory\n```\n\nThe factory for creating dispatch decision promises is pluggable. Ordinarily, `promise.NewWriteOnce` is used.\n\n**Extension Use:** Tests can use a custom factory to instrument or mock promise behavior.\n\n### 6.3 Metrics and Observability Hooks\n\nQueueSet accepts multiple metrics observers:\n- `RatioedGaugePair`: Tracks requests waiting and executing.\n- `RatioedGauge`: Tracks seats in use.\n- `Gauge`: Integrates seat demand over time.\n\n**Extension Use:** Operators can inject custom metrics sinks or route to monitoring systems.\n\n### 6.4 Debug/Dump Interface\n\n**Location:** lines 996\u20131025 in queueset.go\n\n`Dump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump` exposes internal state:\n```go\ntype QueueSetDump struct {\n    Queues              []QueueDump\n    Waiting, Executing  int\n    Dispatched, ...     int\n}\n```\n\n**Extension Use:** Debugging endpoints can pull real-time snapshots; administrators can monitor queue health.\n\n### 6.5 Work Estimator Integration (Upstream)\n\nQueueSet itself doesn't estimate work; it trusts the `WorkEstimate` passed in.\n\n**Extension Point:** The `apf_filter.go` calls a pluggable `workEstimator.EstimateWork()` which can:\n- Account for list size, watch count, mutating payload, etc.\n- Return different seat counts based on priority level.\n\nThis is where heuristics are encoded (e.g., list requests get more seats than get requests).\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications and Failure Handling\n\n### 7.1 Metrics for Monitoring and Alerting\n\nKey metrics emitted by QueueSet (via `metrics/metrics.go`):\n\n1. **`apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total`**\n   - Labels: `reason` (queue-full, concurrency-limit, time-out).\n   - Alert: High rejection rate indicates sustained overload or misconfiguration.\n\n2. **`apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total`**\n   - Rate of requests transitioning from queue to execution.\n   - Alert: Sudden drop may indicate dispatch bug or system stall.\n\n3. **`apiserver_flow_request_wait_duration_seconds`** (histogram)\n   - Time requests spend waiting in queue.\n   - Alert: High percentiles (p99) indicate poor fairness or resource constraint.\n\n4. **`apiserver_flowcontrol_request_concurrency`** (per priority level)\n   - Number of executing requests.\n   - Alert: Consistently at limit suggests under-provisioning or requests holding seats too long.\n\n5. **`apiserver_flowcontrol_priority_level_request_utilization`**\n   - Denominator is ConcurrencyLimit; numerator is actual executing.\n   - Alert: Consistently < 0.5 suggests queuing pressure but low concurrency\u2014possible issue in work estimator or request execution.\n\n6. **`apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total`**\n   - How many times virtual time epoch has been advanced (wrapped).\n   - Alert: Rapid advances on a long-lived server suggest a virtual time leak or very high cumulative concurrency.\n\n### 7.2 Debugging and Troubleshooting\n\n#### Scenario: All requests in a priority level are queued, none dispatching.\n\n**Diagnosis:**\n1. Check if `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit`.\n   - If yes: requests are executing but not finishing; check application logs for hung requests.\n   - If no: bug in dispatch logic or virtual time computation (rare).\n2. Dump the QueueSet via debug endpoint:\n   ```\n   GET /debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_level_state?priority_level=<name>\n   ```\n   Look at `queues[i].NextDispatchR` and `currentR`. If they are very different, a queue may have an inflated virtual start time (anti-windup issue or clock jump).\n\n#### Scenario: One flow is starving others.\n\n**Diagnosis:**\n1. Examine shuffle sharding: are flows hashing to the same queues?\n   - Check `handSize` and `queues` count in config; ensure handSize is set to a reasonable value.\n2. Dump queues: observe if any one queue has disproportionate number of requests from the flow.\n3. Compute virtual finish times manually: `nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()` for each queue. If one queue is consistently lowest, that's correct fairness behavior. If not, virtual time may not be syncing properly.\n\n#### Scenario: Epoch advancing frequently.\n\n**Diagnosis:**\n1. This is expected behavior if cumulative virtual time is high (very high concurrency over time).\n2. Examine `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_r` metric (if available in instrumentation); if it's consistently near `highR`, epochs will advance frequently.\n3. Not a performance issue per se, but indicates the system has been running at high load.\n\n### 7.3 Capacity Planning\n\n#### Choosing DesiredNumQueues\n\n- **Default:** 128 (see bootstrap configs).\n- **Rule of thumb:** \u2248 sqrt(max expected flows) to balance isolation and scheduling overhead.\n  - With K queues, a single misbehaving flow contends with at most HandSize-1 others.\n- **Trade-off:** More queues \u2192 better isolation but more lock contention (round-robin dispatch checks all queues).\n\n#### Choosing QueueLengthLimit\n\n- **Default:** 50.\n- **Formula:** max_queue_length \u2248 (expected request latency) / (max request rate).\n  - If requests take 100ms on average and max rate is 1000 req/s, expect ~100 queued.\n  - Set limit to allow spikes without rejecting under normal variance.\n\n#### Choosing HandSize\n\n- **Default:** 8.\n- **Rule of thumb:** \u2248 sqrt(DesiredNumQueues).\n- **Trade-off:** Larger \u2192 more isolated flows but higher variance in queue load; smaller \u2192 more contention but more even queue depths.\n\n### 7.4 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Lock Contention\n\nQueueSet uses a single mutex protecting all internal state. Each request's `StartRequest()` and `Finish()` acquires this lock.\n\n- **Scaling limit:** Roughly 10k\u2013100k requests/sec per apiserver before lock contention becomes a bottleneck (depends on CPUs, request mix).\n- **Mitigation:** Spread requests across multiple apiservers; partition workloads by priority level.\n\n#### Memory Overhead\n\nEach queued request is a `request{}` struct (~500\u20131000 bytes with embedded fields).\n- **With QueueLengthLimit=50 and DesiredNumQueues=128:** max waiting = 6400 requests = ~6\u201310 MB per priority level.\n- **With multiple priority levels (e.g., 20):** ~100\u2013200 MB for queue state. Not a concern on modern hardware.\n\n#### Virtual Time Computation\n\n`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()` iterates over all queues every sync cycle (on every StartRequest/Finish).\n- **Complexity:** O(DesiredNumQueues).\n- **With 128 queues:** ~2\u20133 \u00b5s per sync, negligible overhead.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 fairqueuing/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go               \u2190 QueueSet, Request, QueueSetFactory interfaces\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset.go            \u2190 queueSet, queue, queueSetFactory impl\n\u2502   \u2502 \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset_test.go       \u2190 Comprehensive fairness tests\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 fifo_list_test.go      \u2190 FIFO and work estimate tests\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 promise/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 promise.go             \u2190 WriteOnce promise impl\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 eventclock/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 eventclock.go          \u2190 EventClock interface\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 real.go                \u2190 Real system clock\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 fake.go                \u2190 Fake clock for testing\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 integrator.go              \u2190 Seat demand integrator\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_filter.go                  \u2190 Entry point, calls QueueSet.StartRequest()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller.go              \u2190 Creates/reconfigs QueueSets\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller_debug.go        \u2190 Debug endpoints for dump\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 request/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 width.go                   \u2190 WorkEstimate struct\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 list_work_estimator.go     \u2190 List request seats\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 mutating_work_estimator.go \u2190 Mutating request seats\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 seat_seconds.go            \u2190 SeatSeconds type and math\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 metrics/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 metrics.go                 \u2190 All APF metrics definitions\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 debug/\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 dump.go                    \u2190 QueueSetDump, QueueDump structs\n```\n\n**Cross-repo dependencies:**\n- `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/` \u2014 Queue assignment sharding.\n- `k8s.io/klog/v2` \u2014 Structured logging (extensive in queueset.go).\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets` \u2014 Set operations for requestsExecuting.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Design Rationale and Algorithmic Notes\n\n### 9.1 Why Fair Queuing for APIs?\n\nTraditional fair queuing was designed for **network packet scheduling**: each flow gets equal share of link bandwidth. APF adapts this to **request handling**, where:\n- Flows are defined by (user, namespace) or other distinguishers.\n- \"Bandwidth\" becomes concurrency (number of simultaneously executing requests).\n- \"Packet size\" becomes request service time (unknown until completion).\n\nThis prevents any single flow from monopolizing the apiserver, which is critical for multi-tenant clusters.\n\n### 9.2 Why Virtual Time?\n\nVirtual time decouples fairness logic from wall-clock time. Instead of scheduling by real-time deadlines, requests are scheduled by their **virtual finish time**\u2014a logical ordering based on virtual work done.\n\n**Advantage:** The algorithm doesn't depend on accurate request latency estimates. If one request takes 10ms and another takes 100ms, virtual time accounts for that.\n\n**Trade-off:** Estimation error (G vs. actual S) leads to transient unfairness, but the retroactive adjustment corrects long-term behavior.\n\n### 9.3 Why Shuffle Sharding?\n\nHead-of-line blocking in a single queue is a classic problem: if one slow request is at the head, all others are blocked. With multiple queues and random shard assignment:\n- A slow request blocks only requests in the same shard.\n- With K queues and hand size H, the probability of blocking is proportional to H/K.\n\nThis is a **randomized isolation** technique, proven effective in networking (e.g., Facebook's Prism, Google's WCMP).\n\n### 9.4 Why Two-Phase Config Change?\n\nTwo phases (BeginConstruction, Complete) allow:\n1. **Validation** before committing resources (prevents partial failures).\n2. **Atomicity:** Either the entire reconfiguration succeeds, or none.\n3. **Flexibility:** Tests and operators can separate queuing logic from dispatching policy.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet is a **sophisticated, fairness-preserving concurrency control system** that adapts classic networking algorithms to API server request queuing. Its core strength is **guaranteed fairness** despite heterogeneous request costs and arrival patterns. The key techniques\u2014virtual time, shuffle sharding, and adaptive sit allocation\u2014work together to provide isolation without requiring per-flow state tracking at the system level.\n\nOperators deploying APF should focus on:\n1. **Choosing queue counts and depths** based on expected traffic patterns.\n2. **Monitoring rejection and wait time metrics** to detect misconfiguration.\n3. **Tuning work estimators** to accurately reflect request cost (in coordination with application teams).\n4. **Partitioning workloads** across priority levels and ensuring borrowing policies match cluster priorities.\n\nFor developers extending APF, the subsystem provides **clean abstractions** (QueueSet interface, pluggable clocks, custom metrics) that enable testing, instrumentation, and experimentation.\n\n---\n\n## References and Source Locations\n\n- **KEP Design:** https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n- **Fair Queuing Paper:** Nagle et al., \"A Generalized Processor Sharing Approach to Flow Control in Integrated Services Networks\" (https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248)\n- **Shuffle Sharding:** Abseil blog, etc.\n\n",
